      <p>
       <b>
        Greater Boston
       </b>
       is the metropolitan region of
       <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">
        New England
       </a>
       encompassing the municipality of
       <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">
        Boston
       </a>
       , the capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">
        U.S. state
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">
        Massachusetts
       </a>
       , and the most populous city in
       <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">
        New England
       </a>
       , as well as its surrounding areas. The region forms the northern arc of the
       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">
        US northeast megalopolis
       </a>
       and as such, Greater Boston can be described as either a
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">
        metropolitan statistical area
       </a>
       (MSA), or as a broader
       <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">
        combined statistical area
       </a>
       (CSA). The MSA consists of most of the eastern third of Massachusetts, excluding the
       <a href="/wiki/South_Coast_(Massachusetts)" title="South Coast (Massachusetts)">
        South Coast region
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod" title="Cape Cod">
        Cape Cod
       </a>
       ; while the CSA additionally includes the municipalities of
       <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_New_Hampshire" title="Manchester, New Hampshire">
        Manchester
       </a>
       (the largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_New_Hampshire" title="List of cities in New Hampshire">
        city in the U.S. state of New Hampshire
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">
        Providence
       </a>
       (the capital and largest city of the U.S. state of
       <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">
        Rhode Island
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Worcester,_Massachusetts" title="Worcester, Massachusetts">
        Worcester, Massachusetts
       </a>
       (the second largest
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_population_in_New_England" title="List of cities by population in New England">
        city in New England
       </a>
       ), as well as the South Coast region and Cape Cod in Massachusetts.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of Greater Boston's most well-known contributions to human civilization involve the region's
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_metropolitan_Boston" title="List of colleges and universities in metropolitan Boston">
        higher education
       </a>
       and medical institutions. Greater Boston has been influential upon American
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States" title="History of the United States">
        history
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States" title="Economy of the United States">
        industry
       </a>
       . The region and the state of Massachusetts are global leaders in
       <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">
        biotechnology
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">
        engineering
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Massachusetts" title="List of colleges and universities in Massachusetts">
        higher education
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">
        finance
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maritime_trade" title="Maritime trade">
        maritime trade
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Over 80% of Massachusetts' population lives in the Greater Boston metropolitan region. Greater Boston is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_metropolitan_statistical_areas" title="List of United States metropolitan statistical areas">
        ranked tenth in population among US metropolitan statistical areas
       </a>
       , home to 4,732,161 people as of the 2014 US Census estimate, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_combined_statistical_areas" title="List of United States combined statistical areas">
        sixth among combined statistical areas
       </a>
       , with a population of 8,099,575.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The area has hosted many people and sites significant to
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States" title="Culture of the United States">
        American culture
       </a>
       and history, particularly
       <a href="/wiki/American_literature" title="American literature">
        American literature
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_family" title="Kennedy family">
        politics
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">
        American Revolution
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Massachusetts" title="Plymouth, Massachusetts">
        Plymouth
       </a>
       was the site of the first colony in New England, founded in 1620 by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pilgrim_Fathers" title="Pilgrim Fathers">
        Pilgrims
       </a>
       , passengers of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mayflower" title="Mayflower">
         Mayflower
        </a>
       </i>
       . In 1692, the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Salem,_Massachusetts" title="Salem, Massachusetts">
        Salem
       </a>
       and surrounding areas experienced one of America's most infamous cases of
       <a href="/wiki/Mass_hysteria" title="Mass hysteria">
        mass hysteria
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Salem_witch_trials" title="Salem witch trials">
        Salem witch trials
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the late 18th century, Boston became known as the "Cradle of Liberty"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       for the agitation there that led to the American Revolution.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Greater Boston region has played a powerful commercial and cultural role in the history of the United States. Before the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">
        American Civil War
       </a>
       , the region was a center for the
       <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States" title="Abolitionism in the United States">
        abolitionist
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Temperance_movement" title="Temperance movement">
        temperance
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Transcendentalism" title="Transcendentalism">
        transcendentalist
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       movements.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2004, Massachusetts became the first U.S. state to legally recognize
       <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Massachusetts" title="Same-sex marriage in Massachusetts">
        same-sex marriage
       </a>
       as a result of
       <a href="/wiki/Goodridge_v._Department_of_Public_Health" title="Goodridge v. Department of Public Health">
        the decision
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Supreme_Judicial_Court" title="Massachusetts Supreme Judicial Court">
        Massachusetts Supreme Judicial Court
       </a>
       in Boston.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNmarriage_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CNNmarriage-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many prominent American political dynasties have hailed from the Boston region, including the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adams_family" title="Adams family">
        Adams
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_family" title="Kennedy family">
        Kennedy
       </a>
       families.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">
        Harvard University
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">
        Cambridge
       </a>
       is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Colonial_Colleges" title="List of Colonial Colleges">
        the oldest institution of higher learning in the United States
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with the largest
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment" title="Financial endowment">
        financial endowment
       </a>
       of any university,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and whose
       <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Law_School" title="Harvard Law School">
        Law School
       </a>
       has spawned a contemporaneous majority of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" title="United States Supreme Court">
        United States Supreme Court
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court_Justice" title="United States Supreme Court Justice">
        Justices
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Kendall_Square" title="Kendall Square">
        Kendall Square
       </a>
       in Cambridge has been called "the most innovative square mile on the planet", in reference to the high concentration of
       <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">
        entrepreneurial
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">
        start-ups
       </a>
       and quality of innovation which have emerged in the vicinity of the square since 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Both Harvard University and the
       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">
        Massachusetts Institute of Technology
       </a>
       , also in Cambridge, have been ranked among the most highly regarded
       <a href="/wiki/Academic_institution" title="Academic institution">
        academic institutions
       </a>
       in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AcademicRanking2_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AcademicRanking2-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span id="Metropolitan_Area_Planning_Council_.28MAPC.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_Area_Planning_Council_(MAPC)">
        Metropolitan Area Planning Council (MAPC)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Metropolitan Area Planning Council (MAPC)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <span id="Metropolitan_Area_Planning_Council">
       </span>
      </p>
      <p>
       The most restrictive definition of the Greater Boston area is the region administered by the Metropolitan Area Planning Council (MAPC).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mapc_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mapc-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The MAPC is a regional planning organization created by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Court_of_Massachusetts" title="General Court of Massachusetts">
        Massachusetts legislature
       </a>
       to oversee transportation infrastructure and economic development concerns in the Boston area. The MAPC includes 101 cities and towns that are grouped into eight subregions. These include most of the area within the region's outer circumferential highway,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I-495_(MA)" title="I-495 (MA)">
        I-495
       </a>
       . In 2013, the population of the MAPC district was 3.2 million, which was 48% of the total population of Massachusetts,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-datacommon_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-datacommon-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in an area of 1,422 square miles (3,680 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mapc_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mapc-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       of which 39% is forested and an additional 11% is water, wetland, or other open space.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mpo-draft2030_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mpo-draft2030-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The eight subregions and their principal towns are: Inner Core (Boston), Minuteman (
       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Route_2" title="Massachusetts Route 2">
        Route 2
       </a>
       corridor),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MetroWest,_Massachusetts" title="MetroWest, Massachusetts">
        MetroWest
       </a>
       (Framingham),
       <a href="/wiki/North_Shore_(Massachusetts)" title="North Shore (Massachusetts)">
        North Shore
       </a>
       (Lynn), North Suburban (Woburn),
       <a href="/wiki/South_Shore_(Massachusetts)" title="South Shore (Massachusetts)">
        South Shore
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Route_3" title="Massachusetts Route 3">
        Route 3
       </a>
       corridor), SouthWest (Franklin), and Three Rivers (Norwood).
      </p>
      <p>
       Notably excluded from the MAPC and its partner planning body, the Boston Region Metropolitan Planning Organization, are the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merrimack_Valley_(Massachusetts)" title="Merrimack Valley (Massachusetts)">
        Merrimack Valley
       </a>
       cities of Lowell, Lawrence, and Haverhill, much of
       <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_County,_Massachusetts" title="Plymouth County, Massachusetts">
        Plymouth County
       </a>
       , and all of
       <a href="/wiki/Bristol_County,_Massachusetts" title="Bristol County, Massachusetts">
        Bristol County
       </a>
       ; these areas have their own regional planning bodies. Bristol County is part of the Greater Boston CSA, as part of the Providence MSA.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="New_England_City_and_Town_Area_.28NECTA.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="New_England_City_and_Town_Area_(NECTA)">
        New England City and Town Area (NECTA)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: New England City and Town Area (NECTA)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MIT_Charles_River_aerial.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3848" data-file-width="5780" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/MIT_Charles_River_aerial.JPG/220px-MIT_Charles_River_aerial.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/MIT_Charles_River_aerial.JPG/330px-MIT_Charles_River_aerial.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/MIT_Charles_River_aerial.JPG/440px-MIT_Charles_River_aerial.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MIT_Charles_River_aerial.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">
          Cambridge
         </a>
         and Boston;
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MIT" title="MIT">
          MIT
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Kendall_Square" title="Kendall Square">
          Kendall Square
         </a>
         in the foreground, and Boston's
         <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Boston" title="Financial District, Boston">
          Financial District
         </a>
         in the background
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_urban_area" title="United States urban area">
        urbanized area
       </a>
       surrounding Boston serves as the core of a definition used by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Census_Bureau" title="US Census Bureau">
        US Census Bureau
       </a>
       known as the
       <a href="/wiki/New_England_city_and_town_area" title="New England city and town area">
        New England city and town area
       </a>
       (NECTA). The set of towns containing the core urbanized area plus surrounding towns with strong social and economic ties to the core area is defined as the
       <b>
        Boston–Cambridge–Nashua, MA–NH Metropolitan NECTA
       </b>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NECTA-principal_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NECTA-principal-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Boston NECTA is further subdivided into several NECTA divisions, which are listed below. The Boston, Framingham, and Peabody NECTA divisions together correspond roughly to the MAPC area. The total population of the Boston NECTA was 4,540,941 (as of 2000).
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Boston–Cambridge–Newton, MA NECTA Division (92 towns)
       </li>
       <li>
        Framingham, MA NECTA Division (12 towns)
       </li>
       <li>
        Peabody–Salem–Beverly, MA NECTA Division (4 towns)
       </li>
       <li>
        Brockton–Bridgewater–Easton, MA NECTA Division (Old Colony region) (8 towns)
       </li>
       <li>
        Haverhill–Newburyport–Amesbury, MA–NH NECTA Division (Merrimack Valley region) (21 towns)
       </li>
       <li>
        Lawrence–Methuen–Salem, MA–NH NECTA Division (part of Merrimack Valley region) (4 towns)
       </li>
       <li>
        Lowell–Billerica–Chelmsford, MA–NH NECTA Division (Northern Middlesex region) (15 towns)
       </li>
       <li>
        Nashua, NH–MA NECTA Division (21 towns)
       </li>
       <li>
        Taunton–Middleborough–Norton, MA NECTA Division (part of Southeastern region) (9 towns)
       </li>
       <li>
        Lynn–Saugus–Marblehead, MA NECTA Division (5 towns)
       </li>
      </ul>

      <p>
       An alternative definition defined by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="United States Office of Management and Budget">
        United States Office of Management and Budget
       </a>
       , using counties as building blocks instead of towns, is the
       <b>
        Boston–Cambridge–Newton, MA–NH Metropolitan Statistical Area
       </b>
       , which is further subdivided into four metropolitan divisions. The metropolitan statistical area had a total population of approximately 4,732,161 as of 2014 and is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_metropolitan_area" title="United States metropolitan area">
        tenth-largest
       </a>
       in the United States. The components of the metropolitan area with their estimated 2012 populations are listed below.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Boston–Cambridge–Newton, MA–NH Metropolitan Statistical Area (4,640,802)
        <ul>
         <li>
          Boston, MA Metropolitan Division (1,926,030)
          <ul>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_County,_Massachusetts" title="Norfolk County, Massachusetts">
             Norfolk County
            </a>
            , Massachusetts (681,845)
           </li>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_County,_Massachusetts" title="Plymouth County, Massachusetts">
             Plymouth County
            </a>
            , Massachusetts (499,759)
           </li>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Suffolk_County,_Massachusetts" title="Suffolk County, Massachusetts">
             Suffolk County
            </a>
            , Massachusetts (744,426)
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          Cambridge–Newton–Framingham, MA Metropolitan Division (2,292,833)
          <ul>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Middlesex_County,_Massachusetts" title="Middlesex County, Massachusetts">
             Middlesex County
            </a>
            , Massachusetts (1,537,215)
           </li>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Essex_County,_Massachusetts" title="Essex County, Massachusetts">
             Essex County
            </a>
            , Massachusetts (755,618)
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          Rockingham County–Strafford County, NH Metropolitan Division (421,939)
          <ul>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Rockingham_County,_New_Hampshire" title="Rockingham County, New Hampshire">
             Rockingham County
            </a>
            , New Hampshire (297,820)
           </li>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Strafford_County,_New_Hampshire" title="Strafford County, New Hampshire">
             Strafford County
            </a>
            , New Hampshire (124,119)
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span id="Combined_Statistical_Area_.28CSA.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Combined_Statistical_Area_(CSA)">
        Combined Statistical Area (CSA)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Combined Statistical Area (CSA)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Providence,_RI_skyline_edit.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1209" data-file-width="3629" height="73" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Providence%2C_RI_skyline_edit.jpg/220px-Providence%2C_RI_skyline_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Providence%2C_RI_skyline_edit.jpg/330px-Providence%2C_RI_skyline_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Providence%2C_RI_skyline_edit.jpg/440px-Providence%2C_RI_skyline_edit.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Providence,_RI_skyline_edit.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Providence, Rhode Island
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A wider functional metropolitan area based on commuting patterns is also defined by the Office of Management and Budget as the
       <b>
        Boston–Worcester–Providence combined statistical area
       </b>
       . This area consists of the metropolitan areas of
       <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_New_Hampshire" title="Manchester, New Hampshire">
        Manchester
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Worcester,_Massachusetts" title="Worcester, Massachusetts">
        Worcester
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">
        Providence
       </a>
       , as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod" title="Cape Cod">
        Cape Cod
       </a>
       , in addition to greater Boston. The total population as of 2014 for the extended region was estimated at 8,099,575. The following areas, along with the above MSA, are included in the combined statistical area, with their estimated 2012 populations:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Worcester, MA–CT, metropolitan statistical area (923,762)
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Worcester_County,_Massachusetts" title="Worcester County, Massachusetts">
           Worcester County
          </a>
          , Massachusetts (806,163)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Windham_County,_Connecticut" title="Windham County, Connecticut">
           Windham County, Connecticut
          </a>
          (117,599)
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Providence_metropolitan_area" title="Providence metropolitan area">
         Providence–Warwick, RI–MA, metropolitan statistical area
        </a>
        (1,601,374)
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Bristol_County,_Massachusetts" title="Bristol County, Massachusetts">
           Bristol County
          </a>
          , Massachusetts (551,082)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Bristol_County,_Rhode_Island" title="Bristol County, Rhode Island">
           Bristol County
          </a>
          , Rhode Island (49,144)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Kent_County,_Rhode_Island" title="Kent County, Rhode Island">
           Kent County
          </a>
          , Rhode Island (164,843)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Newport_County,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport County, Rhode Island">
           Newport County
          </a>
          , Rhode Island (82,036)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Providence_County,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence County, Rhode Island">
           Providence County
          </a>
          , Rhode Island (628,323)
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Washington_County,_Rhode_Island" title="Washington County, Rhode Island">
           Washington County
          </a>
          , Rhode Island (125,946)
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Concord, NH,
        <a href="/wiki/Micropolitan_statistical_area" title="Micropolitan statistical area">
         micropolitan statistical area
        </a>
        (146,761)
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Merrimack_County,_New_Hampshire" title="Merrimack County, New Hampshire">
           Merrimack County
          </a>
          , New Hampshire (146,761)
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Laconia, NH, micropolitan statistical area (60,327)
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Belknap_County,_New_Hampshire" title="Belknap County, New Hampshire">
           Belknap County
          </a>
          , New Hampshire (60,327)
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Manchester–Nashua, NH, metropolitan statistical area (402,922)
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_County,_New_Hampshire" title="Hillsborough County, New Hampshire">
           Hillsborough County
          </a>
          , New Hampshire (402,922)
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Barnstable Town, MA, metropolitan statistical area (215,423)
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Barnstable_County,_Massachusetts" title="Barnstable County, Massachusetts">
           Barnstable County, Massachusetts
          </a>
          (215,423)
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Boston_metropolitan_area">
        Boston metropolitan area
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Boston metropolitan area">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Census Bureau defines the following as principal cities in the Boston NECTA
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NECTA-principal_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NECTA-principal-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       using criteria developed for what the
       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">
        Office of Management and Budget
       </a>
       calls a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Core_Based_Statistical_Area" title="Core Based Statistical Area">
        Core Based Statistical Area
       </a>
       :
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OMB-standards_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-OMB-standards-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">
         Boston
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">
         Cambridge
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Lowell,_Massachusetts" title="Lowell, Massachusetts">
         Lowell
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">
         Providence
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Quincy,_Massachusetts" title="Quincy, Massachusetts">
         Quincy
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Worcester,_Massachusetts" title="Worcester, Massachusetts">
         Worcester
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St._Patrick_Day%27s_Parade,_Scituate_MA.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2046" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/St._Patrick_Day%27s_Parade%2C_Scituate_MA.jpg/220px-St._Patrick_Day%27s_Parade%2C_Scituate_MA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/St._Patrick_Day%27s_Parade%2C_Scituate_MA.jpg/330px-St._Patrick_Day%27s_Parade%2C_Scituate_MA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/St._Patrick_Day%27s_Parade%2C_Scituate_MA.jpg/440px-St._Patrick_Day%27s_Parade%2C_Scituate_MA.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St._Patrick_Day%27s_Parade,_Scituate_MA.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Day_Parade" title="St. Patrick's Day Parade">
          St. Patrick's Day Parade
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Scituate,_Massachusetts" title="Scituate, Massachusetts">
          Scituate, Massachusetts
         </a>
         , in
         <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_County,_Massachusetts" title="Plymouth County, Massachusetts">
          Plymouth County
         </a>
         , the municipality with the highest percentage identifying
         <a href="/wiki/Irish_diaspora" title="Irish diaspora">
          Irish
         </a>
         ancestry in the United States, at 47.5% in 2010.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
          <a href="#cite_note-22">
           [22]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">
          Irish Americans
         </a>
         constitute the largest ethnicity in Greater Boston.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boston_Chinatown_Paifang.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3408" data-file-width="5129" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Boston_Chinatown_Paifang.jpg/220px-Boston_Chinatown_Paifang.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Boston_Chinatown_Paifang.jpg/330px-Boston_Chinatown_Paifang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Boston_Chinatown_Paifang.jpg/440px-Boston_Chinatown_Paifang.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boston_Chinatown_Paifang.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Boston" title="Chinatown, Boston">
          Boston's Chinatown
         </a>
         , with its
         <a href="/wiki/Paifang" title="Paifang">
          paifang
         </a>
         gate, is home to many
         <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans_in_Boston" title="Chinese Americans in Boston">
          Chinese
         </a>
         and also
         <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Americans_in_Boston" title="Vietnamese Americans in Boston">
          Vietnamese
         </a>
         restaurants.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg/220px-Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg/330px-Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg/440px-Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Were_a_gay_and_happy_family_wagon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Boston
         <a href="/wiki/Gay_pride" title="Gay pride">
          gay pride
         </a>
         march, held annually in June
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other">
        Other
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Greater Boston has a sizable Jewish community, estimated at between 210,000 people,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jewglobe_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jewglobe-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 261,000
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or 5–6% of the Greater Boston metro population, compared with about 2% for the nation as a whole. Contrary to national trends, the number of Jews in Greater Boston has been growing, fueled by the fact that 60% of children in Jewish mixed-faith families are raised Jewish, compared with roughly one in three nationally.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jewglobe_28-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-jewglobe-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The City of Boston also has one of the largest
       <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">
        LGBT
       </a>
       populations per capita. It ranks fifth of all major cities in the country (behind San Francisco, and slightly behind
       <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">
        Seattle
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">
        Atlanta
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">
        Minneapolis
       </a>
       respectively), with 12.3% of the city identifying as gay, lesbian, or bisexual.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">
        Higher education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Higher education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boston,_Massachusetts#Education" title="Boston, Massachusetts">
        Boston, Massachusetts § Education
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_metropolitan_Boston" title="List of colleges and universities in metropolitan Boston">
        List of colleges and universities in metropolitan Boston
       </a>
       ; and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Massachusetts" title="List of colleges and universities in Massachusetts">
        List of colleges and universities in Massachusetts
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;max-width:184px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HarvardWidenerLibrary.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/HarvardWidenerLibrary.jpg/180px-HarvardWidenerLibrary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/HarvardWidenerLibrary.jpg/270px-HarvardWidenerLibrary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/HarvardWidenerLibrary.jpg/360px-HarvardWidenerLibrary.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome,_Cambridge_MA.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg/180px-MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg/270px-MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg/360px-MIT_Building_10_and_the_Great_Dome%2C_Cambridge_MA.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
         <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">
          Harvard University
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">
          MIT
         </a>
         are both widely regarded as in the top handful of universities worldwide for academic research in various disciplines.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AcademicRanking2_15-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-AcademicRanking2-15">
           [15]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A long established center of higher education, the area includes many community colleges, two-year schools, and internationally prominent undergraduate and graduate institutions. The graduate schools include highly regarded schools of law, medicine, business, technology, international relations, public health, education, and religion. Greater Boston contains seven
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_research_universities_in_the_United_States" title="List of research universities in the United States">
        R1 Research Institutions
       </a>
       as per the
       <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">
        Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education
       </a>
       . This is, by far, the highest number of such institutions in a single
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">
        Metropolitan Statistical Area
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_statistics">
        Selected statistics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Selected statistics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Changes in
       <a href="/wiki/House_price_index" title="House price index">
        house prices
       </a>
       for the Greater Boston area are publicly tracked on a regular basis using the
       <a href="/wiki/Case%E2%80%93Shiller_index" title="Case–Shiller index">
        Case–Shiller index
       </a>
       ; the statistic is published by
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">
        Standard &amp; Poor's
       </a>
       and is also a component of S&amp;P's 10-city
       <a href="/wiki/Composite_(finance)" title="Composite (finance)">
        composite index
       </a>
       of the value of the residential real estate market.
      </p>

      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annual_events_in_Boston" title="Annual events in Boston">
        Annual sporting events
       </a>
       include:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon" title="Boston Marathon">
         Boston Marathon
        </a>
        , which follows a course from
        <a href="/wiki/Hopkinton,_Massachusetts" title="Hopkinton, Massachusetts">
         Hopkinton
        </a>
        to Boston
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Charles_Regatta" title="Head of the Charles Regatta">
         Head of the Charles Regatta
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenox_Industrial_Tools_301" title="Lenox Industrial Tools 301">
         Lenox Industrial Tools 301
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sylvania_300" title="Sylvania 300">
         Sylvania 300
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Indy_225" title="New Hampshire Indy 225">
         New Hampshire Indy 225
        </a>
        auto races at the
        <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire_Motor_Speedway" title="New Hampshire Motor Speedway">
         New Hampshire Motor Speedway
        </a>
        oval track.
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h3>

        </a>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_and_bus">
        Rail and bus
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Boston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Rail and bus">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="553" data-file-width="904" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg/220px-MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg/330px-MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg/440px-MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MBTA_Commuter_Rail_and_funding_district_map.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The MBTA district, with Commuter Rail lines in purple
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Transportation_Authority" title="Massachusetts Bay Transportation Authority">
         Massachusetts Bay Transportation Authority
        </a>
        (MBTA, generally known as the "T") rapid transit lines:
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Red_Line_(MBTA)" title="Red Line (MBTA)">
           Red Line
          </a>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_Transit" title="Rapid Transit">
           heavy rail
          </a>
          :
          <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">
           Cambridge
          </a>
          –
          <a href="/wiki/Braintree,_Massachusetts" title="Braintree, Massachusetts">
           Braintree
          </a>
          and Boston (
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mattapan,_Massachusetts" title="Mattapan, Massachusetts">
           Mattapan
          </a>
          )
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Orange_Line_(MBTA)" title="Orange Line (MBTA)">
           Orange Line
          </a>
          heavy rail: Boston (
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaica_Plain,_Massachusetts" title="Jamaica Plain, Massachusetts">
           Jamaica Plain
          </a>
          )–
          <a href="/wiki/Malden,_Massachusetts" title="Malden, Massachusetts">
           Malden
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Blue_Line_(MBTA)" title="Blue Line (MBTA)">
           Blue Line
          </a>
          heavy rail: Boston–
          <a href="/wiki/Revere,_Massachusetts" title="Revere, Massachusetts">
           Revere
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(MBTA)" title="Green Line (MBTA)">
           Green Line
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">
           light rail
          </a>
          /
          <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">
           streetcar
          </a>
          : Cambridge–
          <a href="/wiki/Brookline,_Massachusetts" title="Brookline, Massachusetts">
           Brookline
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Newton,_Massachusetts" title="Newton, Massachusetts">
           Newton
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashmont%E2%80%93Mattapan_High_Speed_Line" title="Ashmont–Mattapan High Speed Line">
           Ashmont–Mattapan High Speed Line
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">
           streetcar
          </a>
          :
          <a href="/wiki/Ashmont,_Boston" title="Ashmont, Boston">
           Ashmont
          </a>
          -
          <a href="/wiki/Milton,_Massachusetts" title="Milton, Massachusetts">
           Milton
          </a>
          -
          <a href="/wiki/Mattapan" title="Mattapan">
           Mattapan
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Silver_Line_(MBTA)" title="Silver Line (MBTA)">
           Silver Line
          </a>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bus_Rapid_Transit" title="Bus Rapid Transit">
           Bus Rapid Transit
          </a>
          South Station–Logan Airport and Downtown–
          <a href="/wiki/Dudley_Square_(MBTA_station)" title="Dudley Square (MBTA station)">
           Dudley Square
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/MBTA_Commuter_Rail" title="MBTA Commuter Rail">
         MBTA Commuter Rail
        </a>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Colony_Lines_(MBTA)" title="Old Colony Lines (MBTA)">
           Old Colony Lines
          </a>
          serving Plymouth County
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Providence/Stoughton_Line" title="Providence/Stoughton Line">
           Providence/Stoughton Line
          </a>
          serving northern Bristol County, western Norfolk County, Kent County, and Washington County, connecting to
          <a href="/wiki/Providence,_Rhode_Island" title="Providence, Rhode Island">
           Providence, Rhode Island
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Fairmount_Line" title="Fairmount Line">
           Fairmount Line
          </a>
          shuttle service from
          <a href="/wiki/South_Station" title="South Station">
           South Station
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Line" title="Franklin Line">
           Franklin Line
          </a>
          serving western Norfolk County
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Greenbush_Line" title="Greenbush Line">
           Greenbush Line
          </a>
          serving Boston's South Shore
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Needham_Line" title="Needham Line">
           Needham Line
          </a>
          serving Boston suburbs and
          <a href="/wiki/Needham,_Massachusetts" title="Needham, Massachusetts">
           Needham
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Framingham/Worcester_Line" title="Framingham/Worcester Line">
           Framingham/Worcester Line
          </a>
          serving southwestern Middlesex County, connecting to
          <a href="/wiki/Worcester,_Massachusetts" title="Worcester, Massachusetts">
           Worcester
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Fitchburg_Line" title="Fitchburg Line">
           Fitchburg Line
          </a>
          serving northwestern Middlesex County, connecting to
          <a href="/wiki/Fitchburg,_Massachusetts" title="Fitchburg, Massachusetts">
           Fitchburg
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Lowell_Line" title="Lowell Line">
           Lowell Line
          </a>
          serving northern Middlesex County
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haverhill/Reading_Line" title="Haverhill/Reading Line">
           Haverhill/Reading Line
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Newburyport/Rockport_Line" title="Newburyport/Rockport Line">
           Newburyport/Rockport Line
          </a>
          serving Essex County &amp; Boston's North Shore
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
         Amtrak
        </a>
        service to New York City and Washington, D.C.
       </li>
       <li>
        Amtrak
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Downeaster_(train)" title="Downeaster (train)">
          Downeaster
         </a>
        </i>
        service to
        <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">
         Maine
        </a>
        from
        <a href="/wiki/North_Station" title="North Station">
         North Station
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The first railway line in the United States was in Quincy. See
       <a href="/wiki/Neponset_River" title="Neponset River">
        Neponset River
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The following Regional Transit Authorities have bus service that connects with MBTA commuter rail stations:

        </cite>
        <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Literary+Trail+of+Greater+Boston%3A+A+Tour+of+Sites+in+Boston%2C+Cambridge%2C+and+Concord%2C+Revised+Edition&amp;rft.pub=Commonwealth+Editions&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=1-889833-67-3&amp;rft.aulast=Wilson&amp;rft.aufirst=Susan&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGreater+Boston">
